Proof from Surah al-Mulk for Creation of Actions
Nasafi proves from Quran 67:13-14 that God creates human actions and refutes Mu'tazilite interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Nasafi derives from Quran 67:13-14 an explicit textual proof and a rational indication that God creates all human actions, and how he responds to the Mu'tazilite alternative reading.

Core Idea
God's knowledge of human actions proves He creates them.

In this passage, Imam Nasafi draws on a powerful Quranic verse that links creation and knowledge. He argues that the verse 'Does He who created not know?' provides both an explicit text (nass) and an implied indication (ishara) that God creates all human actions. After establishing his proof, he dismantles the Mu'tazilite attempt to reinterpret the verse as only referring to God's knowledge of created beings, not their actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verse and the claim
Read the verse (67:13-14) and note how Nasafi introduces it: he says it is both an explicit text and an indication that God creates actions.
The verse is the foundation of the proof.
2
Understand the explicit text (nass) proof
Nasafi argues that the verse directly links creation and knowledge: 'Does He who created not know?' means knowledge is built upon creation, so knowledge of actions entails their creation.
He also points out that the verse uses creation to confirm knowledge, showing that creation is more apparent.
3
Analyze the logical indication (ishara)
The indication is that if creation could exist without knowledge, then using creation as evidence for knowledge would be absurd, like claiming knowledge of fiqh while citing irrelevant facts. Therefore, knowledge of the created is a condition or concomitant of the power to create.
This strengthens the proof beyond the text itself.
4
See the refutation of the Mu'tazilite interpretation
The Mu'tazila read 'man' as the object rather than the subject, changing the meaning to 'Does Allah not know whom He created?' Nasafi refutes this by showing that the verse is a threat about actions, so it must refer to knowledge of actions, not just persons.
Their reading either makes the verse about something else or renders it futile.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشهادات المعارف، أما الكتاب فقوله تعالى: ﴿ وَأَسِرُّوا قَوْلَكُمْ أَوِ اجْهَرُوا بِهِ إِنَّهُ عَلِيمٌ بِذَاتِ الصُّدُورِ أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وَهُوَ اللَّطِيفُ الْخَبِيرُ ﴾ فالآية تنص على أنه خالق أفعال العباد، وفيها أيضًا إشارة إلى أن كل خالق ينبغي أن يكون عالمًا بما خلق، أما كونها نصا فظاهر فإنه تعالى أخبر أنه يعلم ما يسر به العبد في قلبه وما يجهر به وقال: أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ وهو بيان أنه هو الخالق لأنه جعل كونه خالقًا مقررا لما أخبر من تعلق علمه به كأنه قال: وهل يتصور أن لا يعلم من خلقه وأبدا ثبته بما هو أظهر منه ولا يرتاب أحد في كون الأفعال معلومة لله تعالى والله تعالى جعل العلم بهذا ثابتاً بثبوت تخليقه له، فكان هذا إخباراً بكونه مخلوقا له ثم بنى لثبوت العلم به على كونه مخلوقا له، ومثل هذا من أظهر ما يستدل به من النصوص. وأما الإشارة فلأنه أثبت علمه بما أسروا أو جهروا بإثبات تخليقه لذلك، ولو جاز التخليق ممن لا علم له بما خلق لم يكن إثبات العلم بإثبات ما يجوز ثبوته بدون العلم حكمة، كمن يقول لآخر: أنا عالم بالفقه والكلام ثم يقول: ألا أعلم أنا ذلك وأنا ابن بزاز؟ أو يقول: وأنا طويل أو قصير أو وأنا عراقي أو حجازي أو يقول: ألا يعلم الفقه ممن هو بطل كمي أو جواد سخي؟ جل الله تعالى أن يثبت علمه بشيء بناء على ما لا يوجب له العلم به، ويجوز تعريه عن العلم فيكون في إثباته سفها مثبتًا الشيء بما لا يجب ثبوته به كالذين يجهلون طرق إثبات الأشياء على منكري ثبوتها، فصح ما ادعينا من ثبوت العلم بالمخلوق شرطًا لثبوت قدرة التخليق أو قرينة لها لا يزيلها بوجه من الوجوه في حال من الأحوال مع ما كانت الآية نصا في إثبات خلق أفعال العباد، فإذا أثبت الله تعالى قول أهل الحق لكتابه نصا وأشار لهم أيضا إلى ما هو المعقول في المسألة نصرة من الله تعالى لحزبه وتأييدًا لدينه بكلا نوعي الحجة أعني بهما السمعي والعقلي، والله تعالى يحق الحق ويبطل الباطل ولو كره المجرمون. وتأويل المعتزلة أن كلمة "من" ليست براجعه إلى الله تعالى وليست هي الفاعلة بفعل يعلم بل هي مفعولة والفاعل مضمر وهو اسم الله تعالى، وتقدير الآية ألا يعلم الله من خلق ثم بعد ذلك يحتمل أن يكون قوله: خلق، فعلاً لله تعالى واقعًا على كلمة "من" فيكون تقدير الآية: ألا يعلم الله من خلقهم، ويحتمل أن يكون قوله: خلق، فعلا لمن فيكون تقدير الآية: ألا يعلم الله من خلق القول وأسره وجهر به، هذا تأويل فاسد بل هو إبطال الآية، فإن الآية وردت مورد التوعد كقوله تعالى: اعْمَلُوا مَا شِئْتُمْ إِنَّهُ بِمَا تَعْمَلُونَ بَصِيرٌ أي أن الله عليم بأقوالكم أسررتم بها أو جهرتم، غير أنه خص المضمر من القول بالعلم لما أن إثبات العلم به إثبات للعلم بما جهر به منه ضرورة وإثبات العلم بذلك إثبات المجازات كما في قوله: اعْمَلُوا مَا شِئْتُمْ وذا ظاهر في مبتذل الكلام ثم خرج قوله: أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ مخرج تقدير العلم بذلك على ما قررنا، ولذا خرج عقيب إثبات العلم به، كما يقال: إنه عالم بأخلاق فلان ومذاهبه وطرائقه وضرابته، ألا يعلم من صحبه مدة عمره وطول حياته؟ ثم ليس في إثبات العلم بمن خلق الله تعالى إثبات للعلم بما لم يخلقه وإن كان فعلاً له، كما ليس في إثبات تخليق الأنفس إثبات تخليق أفعالها عند المعتزلة، فيصير قوله: ﴿أَلَا يَعْلَمُ مَنْ خَلَقَ خاليًا عن الفائدة خارجًا على حكم العبث – جل الله عمن يكون هذا وصف كلامه.
And testimonies of cognitions: as for the Book, His saying the Exalted: 'And conceal your speech or proclaim it; indeed He is Knower of that within the breasts. Does He who created not know, while He is the Subtle, the Aware?' So the verse stipulates that He is the creator of the actions of servants, and in it is also an indication that every creator should be knowing of what He created. As for its being an explicit text, it is apparent: He the Exalted informed that He knows what the servant conceals in his heart and what he proclaims, and said: 'Does He who created not know?' and this is a clarification that He is the Creator because He made His being Creator a confirmation of what He informed of the attachment of His knowledge to it, as if He said: And is it conceivable that He does not know what He created? And He ever established it by what is more apparent than it, and no one doubts that actions are known to Allah the Exalted, and Allah the Exalted made knowledge of this established by the establishment of His creating it. So this was an informing that it is created for Him, then He built the establishment of knowledge of it upon its being created for Him. And like this is among the most apparent things used as evidence from the texts. As for the indication, He established His knowledge of what they concealed or proclaimed by establishing His creation of that. And if creation were permissible from one who has no knowledge of what He created, then establishing knowledge by establishing what is permissible to exist without knowledge would not be wisdom, like one who says to another: I am knowledgeable in jurisprudence and theology, then says: Do I not know that while I am the son of a cloth merchant? Or says: And I am tall or short or I am Iraqi or Hijazi, or says: Does not jurisprudence know from one who is a champion knight or a generous benefactor? Exalted is Allah above establishing His knowledge of something based on what does not necessitate knowledge of it, and allows its divestment from knowledge, so in establishing it there would be foolishness, affirming a thing by what does not necessitate its existence, like those who are ignorant of the methods of proving things to deniers of their existence. So what we claimed is correct: that establishment of knowledge of the created is a condition for establishment of the power of creation, or a concomitant of it that is not removed in any way in any circumstance, while the verse was an explicit text in establishing the creation of actions of servants. So when Allah the Exalted established the statement of the people of truth from His Book as an explicit text and also indicated to them what is rational in the matter, as support from Allah the Exalted for His party and strengthening of His religion with both types of proof, namely the scriptural and the rational, and Allah the Exalted establishes the truth and nullifies falsehood even if the criminals dislike it. The interpretation of the Mu'tazila is that the word 'man' (who) does not refer back to Allah the Exalted and is not the doer of a verb 'knows', but rather it is the object and the doer is implicit and it is the name of Allah the Exalted. And the estimation of the verse is: Does Allah not know whom He created? Then after that it is possible that His saying 'created' is a verb of Allah the Exalted acting upon the word 'man', so the estimation of the verse is: Does Allah not know whom He created? And it is possible that His saying 'created' is a verb for 'man', so the estimation of the verse is: Does Allah not know who created the speech and concealed it and proclaimed it? This interpretation is corrupt; rather it is an annulment of the verse. For the verse came in the context of threat like His saying the Exalted: 'Do what you will; indeed He is Seeing of what you do.' That is, Allah is knowing of your statements, whether you conceal them or proclaim them, except that He specified the concealed part of speech with knowledge because establishing knowledge of it is an establishment of knowledge of what is proclaimed from it necessarily, and establishing knowledge of that is an establishment of metaphors, as in His saying: 'Do what you will.' And this is apparent in the common speech. Then His saying: 'Does He who created not know?' came in the mode of estimation of knowledge of that according to what we have determined. Therefore it came after the establishment of knowledge of it, just as it is said: He is knowledgeable of so-and-so's morals, doctrines, ways, and habits; does he not know who accompanied him for the duration of his life and the length of his life? Then there is not in establishing knowledge of whom Allah created an establishment of knowledge of what He did not create even if it is an action of His, just as there is not in establishing creation of souls an establishment of creation of their actions according to the Mu'tazila. So His saying: 'Does He who created not know?' becomes devoid of benefit, departing on the rule of futility—exalted is Allah above one whose speech has this description.
Source pages p. 873

Commentary
This passage is a combined proof and refutation. The author, Imam Nasafi, begins by citing Quran 67:13-14 as evidence for the Sunni position that God creates human actions. He identifies two layers of proof: an explicit text (nass) and an indication (ishara). The explicit text is that God knows all actions, and He uses His creation of them as the basis for His knowledge. Nasafi interprets 'Does He who created not know?' as meaning that creation necessitates knowledge of what is created, so God's knowledge of human actions proves He creates them. The indication is logical: if creation did not require knowledge, it would be absurd to use creation as evidence for knowledge. He gives examples like a man claiming knowledge of fiqh and kalam while calling himself a cloth merchant's son—this is irrelevant. Similarly, one cannot prove knowledge by something that could exist without knowledge. Thus, knowledge of the created must be a condition or concomitant of the power to create. The author then addresses the Mu'tazilite interpretation. The Mu'tazila claim that the word 'man' (who) in the verse is the object, not the subject: they read 'Does not Allah know whom He created?' or 'Does not Allah know who created the speech?' Nasafi refutes this by showing that the verse is a threat, as in 'Do what you will; indeed He is Seeing.' The purpose is to affirm God's knowledge of all actions, including hidden ones. If 'man' were object, it would only affirm knowledge of the created beings, not their actions. But the context demands knowledge of actions, so the Mu'tazilite reading either makes the verse about something different or futile. He concludes that their interpretation annuls the verse's clear meaning and renders it pointless, which cannot be attributed to God's speech.

Key Terms

إشارة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The word 'man' in 'Does He who created not know?' is the object (whom He created) rather than the subject (He who created), so the verse only affirms God's knowledge of created beings, not that He creates their actions.
Correction: Nasafi argues that the context of threat and the parallel with 'Do what you will' show that the verse is about knowledge of actions. His reading that 'man' is the subject is necessary for the verse to have a meaningful message about creation of actions.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Nasafi, what is the primary argument from Quran 67:13-14 for the creation of human actions?
A) The verse explicitly states that God creates all actions.
B) The verse argues that God's knowledge of actions proves He creates them, because creation entails knowledge.
C) The verse was revealed in the context of threat, showing that actions are created by the people themselves.
D) The verse uses the word 'man' (who) as an object, indicating that God only knows the people, not their actions.

Key Takeaway
The verse 'Does He who created not know?' establishes that God creates human actions because His knowledge of them is evidence of His creative power.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you truly believe that Allah created that action in that moment? How does this belief affect your repentance and your reliance on Him? Will you ask Him to create in you the action of sincere repentance before you even finish this thought?
?
Allah knows the thoughts you conceal in your heart. If His knowledge of them proves He creates them, are you comfortable with that level of divine scrutiny? Does that drive you to purify your inner state? What will you do about a thought you know He has created and knows?
?
The Mu'tazila rejected this truth to protect human free will and divine justice. But Nasafi argues that God's knowledge itself proves creation. Do you think free will and creation of actions can coexist? What does this tension reveal about your need to submit to divine revelation over human logic? Will you submit your understanding to the Quran's clear text today?

Two Evidences That Actions Contradict Intention
Al-Nasafi presents two proofs that actions contradict intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Nasafi uses rational and sensory evidence to prove that humans do not have the power to create their actions.

Core Idea
Actions occur against our intentions, so we are not their creators.

Al-Nasafi begins by asserting that reason itself testifies that the servant does not create his own actions. He offers two clear proofs: one from rational reflection on the unbeliever's worship, and one from sensory experience of pain. Both show that the actual outcome of an action differs from what the agent intends.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about reason's testimony
The passage argues that if humans had creative power, actions would match their intentions. Since they do not, another creator is indicated.
2
Examine the rational evidence of the unbeliever
The unbeliever intends his worship to be good, but it becomes evil, showing his power is not creative.
3
Examine the sensory evidence of pain
A person does not intend to suffer from walking, but pain occurs, again showing actions deviate from intention.
4
Conclude with the proof
The deviation proves that the action is brought into existence by another.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[الثاني: العقل يشهد بعدم قدرة التخليق للعبد] وأما شهادة نفس العقل أن العبد ليست له قدرة التخليق فهي أن أفعال العباد لا تخرج على ما يقصده العبد من الوصف لفعله بل تخرج على ما يضاد ذلك الوصف ولو كان العبد له قدرة الاختراع والإيجاد لأوجده على ما يريده من الوصف ويقصده، وحيث لم يوجد الفعل على وفق مراده، دل أن الموجد لذلك غيره فجعله فعلاً له على الوصف الذي شاء الموجد أن يوجده ويجعله فعلاً للعبد، والعبد تتعلق قدرته بذلك الموجود على الوصف الذي أوجده الموجد. ودليل خروج فعل العبد عن الوصف الذي يقصده العبد وحصوله على وصف لا يقصده، بل يقصد ضده أمران أحدهما ما يعرف امتناع حصول ما قصده من الوصف وحصول ما يضاد الوصف العقل، والآخر يعرف ذلك فيه بالحس. أما ما يعرف فيه ذلك بالعقل فهو أن الكافر يعتقد وجوب عبادة الصنم ويباشر ذلك بجوارحه يريد حصول ذلك كله على صفة الحسن دون القبيح ومعلوم أن حصول ذلك على ما يضاد الحسن وهو القبح لا على الحسن الذي قصده. وأما ما يعرف ذلك فيه بالحس فإن الإنسان يتأذى بالمشي الدائم ويتألم بالقيام الممتد اللازم، وكذا بكل فعل ثابر المرء على اكتسابه وواظب على ارتكابه، ولا شك أن الفعل لا يقصد إليه الفاعل ليتألم به ويتأذى، ومع هذا حصل مؤذيًا متعبًا فصح ما ادعينا من خروج الفعل على ضد ما يقصده العبد من الوصف ما لم يقصده، فإذا لم يوجد على ذلك دل أن له موجد خرج الموجود على ما أراده. يحقق هذا أن خروج الكفر وعبادة الصنم على ما يقصده الكافر من الحسن وصوابًا وطاعة الله تعالى يتقرب بها إليه يضاد الحكمة وينافيها، وخروجه على ما خرج عليه من القبح مما يقتضيه التدبير الصائب والحكمة البالغة. وجوده على هذا الوصف وإن لم يقصده الكافر إما إن كان بالكافر أم بالفعل نفسه بموجب مختار تولى إيجاده عليه، فإن كان بالكافر أوجب ذا جواز حصول جميع الأفعال الحكمية ممن لا يقصد تحيلها، وذا يؤدي إلى القول بالطبائع والنجوم وهو فاسد على أن فساد ذلك متقرر في البداهة وإن لم يؤد ذلك إلى مذهب باطل. وإن كان بالفعل نفسه أوجب ذلك جواز وجود جميع الأفعال الحكمية من السماوات والأرضين بلا موجد قصد إيجادها وتحصيلها، وذا محال. وإن كان بفاعل مختار تولى إيجاده على ما هو عليه من الوصف لصح ما ذهبنا إليه. فإن قالوا هب أن صفة القبح للفعل وكون الفعل مؤذيًا متعبًا تولى غير الكافر والماشي إيجاده ولكن لم قلتم إن إيجاد نفس الكفر والمشي تولى إيجادهما
[Second: The intellect bears witness that the servant does not have the power of creation.] As for the testimony of reason itself that the servant does not have the power of creation, it is that the actions of servants do not come out according to the description that the servant intends for his action, but come out contrary to that description. And if the servant had the power of invention and bringing into existence, he would bring it into existence according to the description he wants and intends. Since the action does not occur according to his wish, it indicates that the one who brings it into existence is other than him. So He made it an action for him with the description that the Bringer into existence willed to bring it into existence and make it an action for the servant. And the servant's power is attached to that existent with the description by which the Bringer brought it into existence. The proof that the servant's action deviates from the description he intends and occurs with a description he does not intend, but intends its opposite, are two things: one is known by reason, the other is known by sense. As for what is known by reason, it is that the unbeliever believes in the obligation of worshipping the idol and performs that with his limbs, wanting all of that to occur with the attribute of good (ḥasan) rather than evil (qabīḥ). It is known that its occurrence is contrary to good, which is evil, not the good he intended. As for what is known by sense, it is that man suffers from continuous walking and is pained by prolonged standing, and likewise every action a person persists in acquiring and continues in committing. There is no doubt that the agent does not intend the action to cause him pain and suffering, yet it occurs as harmful and tiring. So what we claimed is confirmed: the action occurs contrary to the description the servant intends, not what he intended. Since it does not occur accordingly, it indicates that it has a Bringer into existence who brought the existent into existence according to what He willed. This is verified by the fact that the occurrence of disbelief and worship of the idol according to what the unbeliever intends—goodness and correctness and obedience to Allah by which he seeks nearness to Him—contradicts wisdom and conflicts with it. And its occurrence according to what it actually occurs of evil is part of what sound management and perfect wisdom require. Its existence with this description, even if the unbeliever did not intend it, is either from the unbeliever or from the action itself, by a free agent who undertook to bring it into existence. If it is from the unbeliever, then this necessitates the possibility of all wise actions from one who does not intend to produce them, and this leads to the doctrine of natures and stars, which is corrupt, and its corruption is evident to the intellect even if it does not lead to a false doctrine. And if it is from the action itself, then that necessitates the possibility of the existence of all wise [actions, such as] the heavens and the earths, without a Bringer into existence who intended to bring them into existence and produce them, and that is absurd. And if it is from a free agent who undertook to bring it into existence with the description it is, then what we have gone to is correct. If they say: 'Granted that the attribute of evil for the action and the action being harmful and tiring is undertaken by a being other than the unbeliever and the walker, but why do you say that the very bringing into existence of disbelief and walking is undertaken by another to bring them into existence?'
Source pages p. 878

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī) that the servant (al-ʿabd) does not possess the power of creation (qudrat al-takhlīq). The author presents two types of evidence: rational (ʿaql) and sensory (ḥiss). The rational evidence: The unbeliever (kāfir) intends his worship of the idol to be good (ḥasan), but it actually becomes evil (qabīḥ). If he had the power of creation, he would have made it good. Since it is not according to his intention, the creator is other than him. The sensory evidence: A person suffers from continuous walking or standing; he does not intend suffering, but it occurs. So the actual occurrence contradicts his intention, proving another agent. The author then analyzes possible explanations for why an action occurs with a description not intended: either it is caused by the agent himself, by the action itself, or by a free agent. If by the agent, it would allow any agent to produce wise actions without intending them, leading to doctrines of natures and stars, which are false. If by the action itself, it would imply that all wise actions (like the heavens) could exist without an agent, which is absurd. Thus the only coherent explanation is a free agent (al-mujib al-mukhtār) who creates the action with its actual description, confirming the author's position. The passage ends with an objection from opponents: Why cannot the agent of the evil attribute be different from the agent of the substance of the action? The text is cut off before the answer.

Key Terms
العقل (al-ʿaql)
الحس (al-ḥiss)
الكافر (al-kāfir)
الصنم (al-ṣanam)
الحسن (al-ḥasan)
القبح (al-qubḥ)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the servant's power is creative because he often intends his actions, but the fact that actions often deviate from intention shows the opposite.
Correction: Al-Nasafi demonstrates that the very deviation of actions from intention proves the lack of creative power.

Checkpoint
What are the two types of evidence the author uses to prove that the servant does not have the power of creation?
A) Revelation and consensus
B) Reason and sense perception
C) Analogy and scripture
D) Custom and intuition

Key Takeaway
The deviation of actions from intention proves that humans are not the creators of their actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of an action you performed today with a good intention, but the outcome was negative or even sinful. How does this lesson challenge the idea that you are in full control of your actions and their moral value? Will you now examine your assumption that good intentions guarantee good outcomes?
?
When have you experienced pain or exhaustion from an action you freely chose, even though you did not intend to suffer? How does the sensory evidence in this passage force you to acknowledge that your intention alone does not determine the reality of your actions? What does this reveal about your dependence on the Creator?
?
The unbeliever intends his worship as good, but it is evil because it is directed to a false deity. Can you identify an area in your life where you may be persisting in a practice thinking it is good, while it might actually be contrary to what Allah has commanded? How will you submit your intentions to the One who alone determines the true nature of actions?

Divine Attributes

6 min
Why Only a Free Agent Can Create Actions
Al-Nasafi analyses three possible sources for the unintended qualities of actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the only coherent explanation for the unintended qualities of actions is that a free agent (Allah) creates them.

Core Idea
The action's actual description must come from a free creator, not from the human or the action itself.

After establishing that actions contradict intention, Al-Nasafi anticipates objections. He presents three possible explanations for who or what causes the action to occur with its actual description. Through systematic elimination, he shows that the only viable explanation is a free agent who chooses to create the action with that description. This leads to the Maturidi position that all actions are created by Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the verification statement
The author begins by verifying that the unbeliever's action must occur contrary to his intention due to divine wisdom.
2
Understand the three possibilities
The three possibilities are: from the agent himself, from the action itself, or from a free agent.
3
Analyze why the first two are impossible
If from the agent, it would allow producing wise actions without intending them, leading to false doctrines. If from the action itself, it would imply existence without a creator, which is absurd.
The doctrines of natures and stars are rejected.
4
Accept the third as correct
Thus the action must be from a free agent, which is Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[الثاني: العقل يشهد بعدم قدرة التخليق للعبد] وأما شهادة نفس العقل أن العبد ليست له قدرة التخليق فهي أن أفعال العباد لا تخرج على ما يقصده العبد من الوصف لفعله بل تخرج على ما يضاد ذلك الوصف ولو كان العبد له قدرة الاختراع والإيجاد لأوجده على ما يريده من الوصف ويقصده، وحيث لم يوجد الفعل على وفق مراده، دل أن الموجد لذلك غيره فجعله فعلاً له على الوصف الذي شاء الموجد أن يوجده ويجعله فعلاً للعبد، والعبد تتعلق قدرته بذلك الموجود على الوصف الذي أوجده الموجد. ودليل خروج فعل العبد عن الوصف الذي يقصده العبد وحصوله على وصف لا يقصده، بل يقصد ضده أمران أحدهما ما يعرف امتناع حصول ما قصده من الوصف وحصول ما يضاد الوصف العقل، والآخر يعرف ذلك فيه بالحس. أما ما يعرف فيه ذلك بالعقل فهو أن الكافر يعتقد وجوب عبادة الصنم ويباشر ذلك بجوارحه يريد حصول ذلك كله على صفة الحسن دون القبيح ومعلوم أن حصول ذلك على ما يضاد الحسن وهو القبح لا على الحسن الذي قصده. وأما ما يعرف ذلك فيه بالحس فإن الإنسان يتأذى بالمشي الدائم ويتألم بالقيام الممتد اللازم، وكذا بكل فعل ثابر المرء على اكتسابه وواظب على ارتكابه، ولا شك أن الفعل لا يقصد إليه الفاعل ليتألم به ويتأذى، ومع هذا حصل مؤذيًا متعبًا فصح ما ادعينا من خروج الفعل على ضد ما يقصده العبد من الوصف ما لم يقصده، فإذا لم يوجد على ذلك دل أن له موجد خرج الموجود على ما أراده. يحقق هذا أن خروج الكفر وعبادة الصنم على ما يقصده الكافر من الحسن وصوابًا وطاعة الله تعالى يتقرب بها إليه يضاد الحكمة وينافيها، وخروجه على ما خرج عليه من القبح مما يقتضيه التدبير الصائب والحكمة البالغة. وجوده على هذا الوصف وإن لم يقصده الكافر إما إن كان بالكافر أم بالفعل نفسه بموجب مختار تولى إيجاده عليه، فإن كان بالكافر أوجب ذا جواز حصول جميع الأفعال الحكمية ممن لا يقصد تحيلها، وذا يؤدي إلى القول بالطبائع والنجوم وهو فاسد على أن فساد ذلك متقرر في البداهة وإن لم يؤد ذلك إلى مذهب باطل. وإن كان بالفعل نفسه أوجب ذلك جواز وجود جميع الأفعال الحكمية من السماوات والأرضين بلا موجد قصد إيجادها وتحصيلها، وذا محال. وإن كان بفاعل مختار تولى إيجاده على ما هو عليه من الوصف لصح ما ذهبنا إليه. فإن قالوا هب أن صفة القبح للفعل وكون الفعل مؤذيًا متعبًا تولى غير الكافر والماشي إيجاده ولكن لم قلتم إن إيجاد نفس الكفر والمشي تولى إيجادهما

?

?

?
If every unintended quality of your actions is created by Allah, what does that say about your control over the results of your efforts? How can you submit to His decree in the external outcomes while still striving with pure intention? Will you today surrender a past failure to His wisdom?

When the Objection of Multiple Creators Applies
Author explains condition for valid objection of multiple creators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the condition under which the objection of multiple creators (tawallud) is conceivable and why it does not apply to accidents.

Core Idea
The objection of multiple creators only works when attributes are separable from the subject.

In theological debates about creation, one might object that an act could be produced by multiple agents—one creating the attribute, another the subject. This objection, however, is not universally valid. In this passage, the author specifies when such an objection is even conceivable and when it fails outright.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice the contrast between 'bodies and their attributes' and 'accidents whose attributes return to their essences'.
2
Identify the condition for the objection
The passage says the objection 'is only realized when the attribute is beyond the meaning of the described.' Identify what this means: a separable attribute.
Example: a body's color is separate from the body itself.
3
Understand the exception for accidents
The passage then says for accidents, 'such speech is not valid' because their attributes are not separate but return to their essences. Grasp why this distinction matters.
Accidents like existence or motion have no independent attribute.
4
Test your understanding
Use the checkpoint question to check if you can apply the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير الكافر والماشي؟ قيل : هذا السؤال إنما يتحقق فيما كانت الصفة وراء معنی الموصوف، كما فى الأجسام وصفاتها فيتخبط إنسان فيقول: تولى فاعل إيجاد الصفة وآخر إيجاد الموصوف فلا يكون محيلاً في نفس الدعوى، وإن كان الدليل يوجب لدى التحقيق فساد قول من يدعي تعدد الموجدين، فأما في الأعراض التي كانت صفاتها في الحقيقة راجعة إلى ذواتها فلا يستقيم مثل هذا الكلام.
Other than the disbeliever and the walker? It was said: This question is only realized when the attribute is beyond the meaning of the described, as in bodies and their attributes, so a person becomes confused and says: One agent undertakes the creation of the attribute and another the creation of the described, so it is not impossible in the claim itself, even if the proof requires upon investigation the corruption of the statement of one who claims multiplicity of creators. As for accidents whose attributes in reality return to their essences, such speech is not valid.
Source pages p. 880

Commentary
This passage is an answer to an implicit objection about the creation of acts by multiple agents. The author explains that the objection that an act could be created by two agents (one creating the attribute, another creating the subject) only makes sense when the attribute is separate from the subject, as in bodies and their attributes. In such a case, even though the objection might be conceivable, upon investigation it is proven false. However, in the case of accidents (non-substantial entities), their attributes are not separate but return to their essences. Thus, the objection does not apply, because the attribute and the essence are not distinct enough to be assigned to different creators.

Key Terms
صفة
موصوف
أعراض
ذوات
إيجاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the objection of multiple creators applies universally to all created things.
Correction: The passage explains that the objection only applies when attributes are separable from the subject, as in bodies. For accidents, the objection is invalid because attributes are not distinct.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in what case is the objection of multiple creators conceivable?
A) When the attribute is inherent to the described
B) When the attribute is separate from the described
C) Only in the case of bodies
D) In all cases

Key Takeaway
The objection of multiple creators is only conceivable when attributes are separable from their subjects; for accidents, it is invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness the beauty of creation—like a sunset or a child's smile—do you ever mentally separate the creation into parts and assign each to different 'causes'? How does this lesson call you to redirect that tendency toward the One Creator?
?
Think of a blessing in your life that you typically attribute to your own effort or another person. Can you see that blessing as an accident whose 'attribute' is inherent to its essence, making it impossible to split the creation? What does that demand from you in gratitude?
?
If the objection of multiple creators is only conceivable when attributes are separable, then how often do you treat God's attributes (like mercy or power) as if they could be separated from His essence? What practical change in your worship does this insight require?

Six Absurdities from Ascribing Creative Power to Others
Nasafi lists six absurdities resulting from ascribing creative power to others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six logical absurdities that al-Nasafi argues follow from attributing creative power to any being other than God.

Core Idea
Claiming creatures create leads to six irreconcilable contradictions about God and creation.

Al-Nasafi presents a powerful argument by contradiction. If someone claims that a creature can truly create, then a cascade of impossible consequences follows. In this passage, he lists six such absurdities. Each one, if examined, shows that the original claim is rationally untenable. Read the list carefully — later he will unpack each one.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the repeated word 'منها' which introduces each absurdity.
There are exactly six items.
2
Understand the first two absurdities
The first absurdity is that it implies God is either incapacitated or prevented. The second is that it destroys the standard proofs for tawḥīd.
These attack God's power and the rational evidence for His oneness.
3
Understand the next four absurdities
The third absurdity leads to two creators. The fourth implies God was not eternally powerful. The fifth creates similarity between divine and creaturely acts. The sixth makes worshipping God alone logically permissible.
Each consequence is more severe than the last.
4
Reflect on the method
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument. The premise (creatures have creative power) is shown to entail contradictions, so the premise must be false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث: إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تؤدي إلى مجموعة من المحالات. وأما دعوانا أن إثبات قدرة التخليق لغير الله تعالى يؤدي إلى المحال فدعوى صحيحة، وعند الكشف عن ذلك تبين أن ذلك يؤدي إلى ضروب من المحال منها: أنه يؤدي إلى القول بتعجيز الله تعالى أو كونه ممنوعًا. ومنها: أنه يؤدي إلى إبطال دلائل الموحدين على توحيد الصانع وتعجيز الموحدين عن إثبات وحدانية الصانع جل وعلا. ومنها: أن وجود محدث لم يوجده الله تعالى ولم يكن له عليه القدرة يؤدي إلى كون العالم بصانعين. ومنها: أنه يؤدي إلى أن تكون القدرة من صفات الفعل على مذاهب الخصوم، ويلزم على ذلك أنه لم يكن في الأزل قادرًا عندهم. ومنها: أنه يؤدي إلى وقوع التشابه بين فعل القديم والمحدث. ومنها: أنه يؤدي إلى جواز عبادة الله تعالى.
Third: Proving creative power for other than God leads to a group of absurdities. As for our claim that proving creative power for other than God Almighty leads to absurdity, it is a correct claim. Upon investigation it becomes clear that this leads to various kinds of absurdity, among them: that it leads to saying that God Almighty is incapacitated or prevented. Among them: that it leads to invalidating the proofs of the monotheists concerning the oneness of the Maker and incapacitating the monotheists from proving the oneness of the Maker, Glorious and Exalted. Among them: that the existence of a temporal thing that God did not bring into existence and had no power over it leads to the world having two makers. Among them: that it leads to power being among the attributes of action according to the doctrines of the opponents, and it necessarily follows from that that He was not eternally powerful according to them. Among them: that it leads to the occurrence of resemblance between the action of the Eternal and the temporal. Among them: that it leads to the permissibility of worshipping God Almighty.
Source pages p. 882

Commentary
This passage enumerates six absurd consequences that result from the Mu'tazilite claim that creatures can possess creative power (qudrat al-takhlīq). The author presents this as the third major argument in the section. He lists each consequence without yet explaining how each follows. The six are: (1) it implies that God is either incapacitated (ta'jīz) or prevented (man') from acting; (2) it undermines the standard proofs of tawḥīd and disables monotheists from demonstrating the oneness of the Creator; (3) it entails that a temporal thing exists without God creating it, leading to belief in two creators; (4) it implies that power is an attribute of action according to the opponents, meaning God was not eternally powerful; (5) it creates an unacceptable similarity between divine and creaturely acts; and (6) it leads to the permissibility of worshipping God in a manner that suggests plurality. The passage serves as a preview; the author then proceeds to demonstrate each point individually.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These six absurdities are separate unrelated arguments against the Mu'tazila.
Correction: They are all logical consequences of a single premise: that a creature can have creative power. The list demonstrates that this single premise leads to multiple contradictions.

Checkpoint
How many absurdities does al-Nasafi list as following from attributing creative power to other than God?
A) Three
B) Five
C) Six
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Attributing creative power to creatures leads to at least six absurdities, proving that such power belongs exclusively to God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your daily reliance on people, money, or your own abilities, do you ever catch yourself treating these means as if they have independent creative power—forgetting that only God truly creates outcomes? How would your heart change if you genuinely believed that no one but God can bring about any effect?
?
The sixth absurdity warns that if creatures could create, worshipping God alone would become merely permissible, not necessary. Examine your prayer and worship: is it driven by a deep conviction that God alone deserves all worship, or do you sometimes worship out of habit or social expectation? What would it take for your worship to become truly exclusive and heartfelt?
?
One of the absurdities is blurring the distinction between the Creator and creation. In your daily thoughts, do you ever subtly elevate creation (a leader, an imam, a scholar, or even your own desires) to a status that rivals God’s authority? What concrete step can you take today to restore the clear line between the Eternal and the temporal in your heart?
